  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>Trying to create a database with the following URL (note the Chinese character in the database name):</p> 
                  <p>jdbc:derby://localhost:1527/\u4e10;create=true</p> 
                  <p>throws the following exception:</p> 
                  <p>----<del>%&lt;</del>----<br> Exception in thread "main" org.apache.derby.client.am.SqlException: Unicode string can't convert to Ebcdic string<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.EbcdicCcsidManager.convertFromUCS2(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.Request.writeScalarPaddedString(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnectionRequest.buildRDBNAM(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnectionRequest.buildACCSEC(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnectionRequest.writeAccessSecurity(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnection.writeServerAttributesAndKeyExchange(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnection.flowServerAttributesAndKeyExchange(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnection.flowUSRIDONLconnect(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnection.flowConnect(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.client.net.NetConnection.&lt;init&gt;(Unknown Source)<br> at org.apache.derby.jdbc.ClientDriver.connect(Unknown Source)<br> at java.sql.DriverManager.getConnection(DriverManager.java:525)<br> at java.sql.DriverManager.getConnection(DriverManager.java:193)<br> at jdbctest.Main.main(Main.java:33)<br> ----<del>%&lt;</del>----</p> 
                  <p>It's possible, however, to create databases using the embedded driver, using an URL like:</p> 
                  <p>jdbc:derby:\u4e10;create=true</p> 
                  <p>Tested with both 10.1.1.0 and 10.1.2.1 with the same result.</p> 
                  <p>Complete code to reproduce the bug:</p> 
                  <p>----<del>%&lt;</del>----<br> public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {<br> Class.forName("org.apache.derby.jdbc.ClientDriver");<br> Connection conn = DriverManager.getConnection("jdbc:derby://localhost:1527/\u4e10;create=true");<br> }<br> ----<del>%&lt;</del>----</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eJust one quick comment here. I once started looking at this issue and I i got some way towards a solution. My impression from looking at the DRDA spec is that it may not be THEORETICALLY possible (because of limitations such as those mentioned by Kathey), but in PRACTICE there should be possible to extend Derby\'s driver to use a different encoding and fall back to the old behavior when connected to an old server. It should be simple to make the server compatible with the new Derby client, old Derby client, DB2 client or the ODBC client. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think I still have the work that I did on this lying around. I can try to make a patch of it, but I can\'t guarantee that the patch can be made against the latest trunk. That patch would by no means be a polished solution, but could perhaps be a starting point...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dyret\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12655228_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dyret\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dyret\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Dyre Tjeldvoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12655228_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'10\\/Dec\\/08 14:40\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-12-10T14:40:10+0000\'\u003e10\\/Dec\\/08 14:40\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Just one quick comment here. I once started looking at this issue and I i got some way towards a solution. My impression from looking at the DRDA spec is that it may not be THEORETICALLY possible (because of limitations such as those mentioned by Kathey), but in PRACTICE there should be possible to extend Derby\'s driver to use a different encoding and fall back to the old behavior when connected to an old server. It should be simple to make the server compatible with the new Derby client, old Derby client, DB2 client or the ODBC client.  \\n\\n I think I still have the work that I did on this lying around. I can try to make a patch of it, but I can\'t guarantee that the patch can be made against the latest trunk. That patch would by no means be a polished solution, but could perhaps be a starting point... \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12655235\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12655235&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12655235\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dyret\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12655235_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dyret\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dyret\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Dyre Tjeldvoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12655962_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Dec\\/08 10:34\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-12-12T10:34:28+0000\'\u003e12\\/Dec\\/08 10:34\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHi Kathey, \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003emy work on this issue should be in the patch. Once the negotiating is working you just need to go through the code to find all the places where it is assumed that a given string length will fit in the same number of bytes. That isn\'t too bad as I recall, but there are some sticky points where a string, encoded in the negotiated charset, should be placed in DRDA fields which are specified with a fixed BYTE size, and should be padded to the correct size with space chars. This is simple as long as you can rely on the space character fitting in one byte, but when supporting encodings such as UCS-2 where space is two bytes, you can no longer use Arrays.fill() directly...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI also think there is a DRDA field where you are supposed to fill in the client\'s ip-address (or part of it) as a string in the negotiated charset, and that the number of bytes you can use is not enough to encode in UCS-2. But I think I concluded that this field is not used for anything important, so deviating from the spec here should not be a problem... \u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dyret\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12655962_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dyret\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dyret\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Dyre Tjeldvoll\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12655962_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Dec\\/08 10:34\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-12-12T10:34:28+0000\'\u003e12\\/Dec\\/08 10:34\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Hi Kathey,  \\n\\n my work on this issue should be in the patch. When working on it, I didn\'t really aim for a minimal solution, so it may be possible to achieve this with less work than what my patch suggests. \\n\\n Based on what I can remember it seems like you are on the right track. Once the negotiating is working you just need to go through the code to find all the places where it is assumed that a given string length will fit in the same number of bytes. That isn\'t too bad as I recall, but there are some sticky points where a string, encoded in the negotiated charset, should be placed in DRDA fields which are specified with a fixed BYTE size, and should be padded to the correct size with space chars. This is simple as long as you can rely on the space character fitting in one byte, but when supporting encodings such as UCS-2 where space is two bytes, you can no longer use Arrays.fill() directly... \\n\\n I also think there is a DRDA field where you are supposed to fill in the client\'s ip-address (or part of it) as a string in the negotiated charset, and that the number of bytes you can use is not enough to encode in UCS-2. But I think I concluded that this field is not used for anything important, so deviating from the spec here should not be a problem...               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12661713\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12661713&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12661713\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"kmarsden\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12661713_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=kmarsden\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"kmarsden\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kathey Marsden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12661713_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'07\\/Jan\\/09 21:21\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2009-01-07T21:21:12+0000\'\u003e07\\/Jan\\/09 21:21\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI have been talking with the local DRDA experts and found out that they are working on a new DRDA ACR for a UNICODEMGR which I think can help us with this issue.  The  short summary is this:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eEXCSAT and ACCSEC are always sent EBCDIC.  As part of the MGRLVL exchange,  client sends UNICODEMGR 1208 which means that it is requesting all additional DDM parameters will be exchanged in code page 1208.  The server responds with UNICODEMGR 1208 if it can accommodate the request.  Otherwise it responds with UNICODEMGR 0 and all DDM parameters will continue to be exchanged in EBCDIC.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOne problem with this approach is that ACCSEC currently has an RDBNAM parameter which we treat as required (the spec lists it as optional) and that has to be sent EBCDIC.  So, my proposal is that we use the UNICODEMGR and we send  RDBNAM on ACCSEC \u003cb\u003eonly if\u003c\\/b\u003e  the EBCDIC conversion can be done.   If the conversion can\'t be done, we send no RDBNAM on ACCSEC.  Then we change the server to use the RDBNAM sent with the unicode  SECCHK instead of the one sent on ACCSEC.   (Currently we just verify that the SECCHK RDBNAM is the same as the one that was sent on ACCSEC.)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor an old client working with a new server, there will be no regression and the error message on sending a database name with international characters will be the same as currently listed in \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728\\\" title=\\\"Unable to create databases whose name containg Chinese characters through the client driver\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-728\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-728\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor a new client working with a old server, this will mean that  all the cases that currently pass will still pass, but if a nonconvertible database name is sent (e,g, one with Chinese \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ncharacters) , the server will send back a SYNTAXRM and the \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nserver console will show:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n  = 2110; Error Code Value = e. Plaintext connection attempt \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nfrom an SSL enabled client?\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAProtocolException: Execution \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nfailed because of a Distributed Protocol Error:  DRDA_Proto_\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSYNTAXRM; CODPNT arg  = 2110; Error Code Value = e. Plaintext \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nconnection attempt from an SSL enabled client?\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        at \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.throwSyntaxrm(DRDAConn\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThread.java:513)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        at \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.missingCodePoint(DRDAC\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nonnThread.java:543)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        at \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.parseACCSEC(DRDAConnTh\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nread.java:1948)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        at \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.processCommands(DRDACo\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nnnThread.java:943)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        at \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.run(DRDAConnThread.jav\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\na:290)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe client could intercept the SYNTAXRM and  knowing it was unable to convert the RDBNAM to EBCDIC could throw the same message it does now.  The only regression  would be that users attempting to send an invalid database name would now see the server side protocol error occur. I think it  is an acceptable regression, since it won\'t cause any working  cases to fail even with mixed revision server\\/client and it will enable us to move forward and have internationalized  database name, user and password.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI prototyped the change and it all seemed to work ok.  I\'ll attach the prototype patch.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI  would like to implement as much as possible of this for 10.5, but since approval of the ACR by opengroup won\'t happen by the time we release 10.5, I propose to make the implementation dependent on a client system property derby.drda.unicodemgr=true.  This would be false by default but could be switch to true in a maintenance release once opengroup approval occurs. Currently the hope is to have the ACR available publicly by the end of January.  Then I would need Rick\'s help to try to push it through opengroup since he is our opengroup rep.  I don\'t know how long that takes.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"kmarsden\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12661713_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=kmarsden\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"kmarsden\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kathey Marsden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12661713_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'07\\/Jan\\/09 21:21\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2009-01-07T21:21:12+0000\'\u003e07\\/Jan\\/09 21:21\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I have been talking with the local DRDA experts and found out that they are working on a new DRDA ACR for a UNICODEMGR which I think can help us with this issue.  The  short summary is this: \\n\\n EXCSAT and ACCSEC are always sent EBCDIC.  As part of the MGRLVL exchange,  client sends UNICODEMGR 1208 which means that it is requesting all additional DDM parameters will be exchanged in code page 1208.  The server responds with UNICODEMGR 1208 if it can accommodate the request.  Otherwise it responds with UNICODEMGR 0 and all DDM parameters will continue to be exchanged in EBCDIC. \\n\\n One problem with this approach is that ACCSEC currently has an RDBNAM parameter which we treat as required (the spec lists it as optional) and that has to be sent EBCDIC.  So, my proposal is that we use the UNICODEMGR and we send  RDBNAM on ACCSEC  only if   the EBCDIC conversion can be done.   If the conversion can\'t be done, we send no RDBNAM on ACCSEC.  Then we change the server to use the RDBNAM sent with the unicode  SECCHK instead of the one sent on ACCSEC.   (Currently we just verify that the SECCHK RDBNAM is the same as the one that was sent on ACCSEC.) \\n\\n For an old client working with a new server, there will be no regression and the error message on sending a database name with international characters will be the same as currently listed in  \\n  DERBY-728  . \\n\\n For a new client working with a old server, this will mean that  all the cases that currently pass will still pass, but if a nonconvertible database name is sent (e,g, one with Chinese  \\ncharacters) , the server will send back a SYNTAXRM and the  \\nserver console will show: \\n  = 2110; Error Code Value = e. Plaintext connection attempt  \\nfrom an SSL enabled client? \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAProtocolException: Execution  \\nfailed because of a Distributed Protocol Error:  DRDA_Proto_ \\nSYNTAXRM; CODPNT arg  = 2110; Error Code Value = e. Plaintext  \\nconnection attempt from an SSL enabled client? \\n        at  \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.throwSyntaxrm(DRDAConn \\nThread.java:513) \\n        at  \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.missingCodePoint(DRDAC \\nonnThread.java:543) \\n        at  \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.parseACCSEC(DRDAConnTh \\nread.java:1948) \\n        at  \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.processCommands(DRDACo \\nnnThread.java:943) \\n        at  \\norg.apache.derby.impl.drda.DRDAConnThread.run(DRDAConnThread.jav \\na:290) \\n\\n\\n The client could intercept the SYNTAXRM and  knowing it was unable to convert the RDBNAM to EBCDIC could throw the same message it does now.  The only regression  would be that users attempting to send an invalid database name would now see the server side protocol error occur. I think it  is an acceptable regression, since it won\'t cause any working  cases to fail even with mixed revision server\\/client and it will enable us to move forward and have internationalized  database name, user and password.   \\n\\n I prototyped the change and it all seemed to work ok.  I\'ll attach the prototype patch. \\n\\n I  would like to implement as much as possible of this for 10.5, but since approval of the ACR by opengroup won\'t happen by the time we release 10.5, I propose to make the implementation dependent on a client system property derby.drda.unicodemgr=true.  This would be false by default but could be switch to true in a maintenance release once opengroup approval occurs. Currently the hope is to have the ACR available publicly by the end of January.  Then I would need Rick\'s help to try to push it through opengroup since he is our opengroup rep.  I don\'t know how long that takes. \\n\\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12661729\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12661729&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12661729\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"kmarsden\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12661729_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=kmarsden\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"kmarsden\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kathey Marsden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12700281&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12700281\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=rhillegas\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"rhillegas\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Rick Hillegas\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12700281_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'17\\/Apr\\/09 18:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2009-04-17T18:52:15+0000\'\u003e17\\/Apr\\/09 18:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHi Kathey,\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThanks for attaching the proposed change to Volume 1 of the DRDA spec. It got me thinking about SQL identifiers. It seems from the changes to chapters 6 and 7 on page 5 that DRDA still thinks that sql identifiers are limited to 255 bytes. I don\'t know where this limitation actually surfaces. It doesn\'t surface in the simple test I have attached (BigTableName) which pokes and peeks a table whose schema name and table name are each 128 unicode characters long, represented in utf-8 as 384 bytes apiece.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut it may prevent us from extending our DRDA or SQL support in the future. The maximum length of a SQL identifier is 128 unicode characters, according to part 2 of the 2008 SQL Standard, section 5.2 (&lt;token&gt; and &lt;separator&gt;), syntax rule (13). Derby supports this maximum length. At two bytes per Java character, this works out to 256 bytes, not 255. Since each unicode character can potentially expand to 4 bytes in UTF-8 encoding, the maximum length of a UTF-8 encoded identifier is 512 bytes. I believe that DRDA\'s sql identifiers should be at least 256 bytes long and probably 512 bytes.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThanks.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"rhillegas\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12700281_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=rhillegas\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"rhillegas\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Rick Hillegas\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12700281_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'17\\/Apr\\/09 18:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2009-04-17T18:52:15+0000\'\u003e17\\/Apr\\/09 18:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Hi Kathey, \\n\\n Thanks for attaching the proposed change to Volume 1 of the DRDA spec. It got me thinking about SQL identifiers. It seems from the changes to chapters 6 and 7 on page 5 that DRDA still thinks that sql identifiers are limited to 255 bytes. I don\'t know where this limitation actually surfaces. It doesn\'t surface in the simple test I have attached (BigTableName) which pokes and peeks a table whose schema name and table name are each 128 unicode characters long, represented in utf-8 as 384 bytes apiece. \\n\\n But it may prevent us from extending our DRDA or SQL support in the future. The maximum length of a SQL identifier is 128 unicode characters, according to part 2 of the 2008 SQL Standard, section 5.2 (&lt;token&gt; and &lt;separator&gt;), syntax rule (13). Derby supports this maximum length. At two bytes per Java character, this works out to 256 bytes, not 255. Since each unicode character can potentially expand to 4 bytes in UTF-8 encoding, the maximum length of a UTF-8 encoded identifier is 512 bytes. I believe that DRDA\'s sql identifiers should be at least 256 bytes long and probably 512 bytes. \\n\\n Thanks.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12700286\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12700286&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12700286\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"kmarsden\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12700286_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=kmarsden\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"kmarsden\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kathey Marsden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI was recently discussing UNICODEMGR implementation with some engineers working on other database products.  The topic of the encoding for embedded character data in PRDDTA and CRRTKN came up.  The fields themselves are architected in DRDA as BYTSTRDR - Byte String, but do contain character data.  The question was whether the character data should be UNICODE  if UNICODEMGR was being used or should remain EBCDIC.  I was asked how it will be in Derby\'s implemenation. I think it should be UNICODE. It just makes more sense (to me)  and is how the current code will work, but should be limited to single byte characters.   Let me know if you have a different opinion or better ideas.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"kmarsden\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12867328_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=kmarsden\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"kmarsden\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kathey Marsden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12867328_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/May\\/10 00:13\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-05-14T00:13:30+0000\'\u003e14\\/May\\/10 00:13\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I was recently discussing UNICODEMGR implementation with some engineers working on other database products. Espinha\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12877191_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Jun\\/10 20:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-06-09T20:33:26+0000\'\u003e09\\/Jun\\/10 20:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI need to brainstorm a bit here regarding the Utf8CcsidManager class that I have.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere\'s one thing that I didn\'t implement because of a detail regarding the following method:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npublic String convertToUCS2(byte[] sourceBytes, int offset, int numToConvert) { }\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo far we had this method on the EbcdicCcsidManager and then it\'s fine because EBCDIC only uses one byte per character at all times. So the offset parameter always works in a consistent way, that is to say that if offset is 5, we are not only getting 5 sourceBytes but also getting exactly 5 characters.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, when we come to an Utf8CcsidManager, this offset might land straight in the middle of a character; then if we cut a character in half byte-wise, we will end with a totally different character.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIs it acceptable to consider offset as a number of characters rather than a number of bytes? It works both ways in EBCDIC but for UTF8 it would mean converting the sourceBytes to a String, offsetting it character-wise, and then convert the \\u00ABoffsetted\\u00BB String to UCS2.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAny other ideas anyone might have?\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"espinha\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12877191_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=espinha\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"espinha\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Tiago R. Espinha\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12877191_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Jun\\/10 20:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-06-09T20:33:26+0000\'\u003e09\\/Jun\\/10 20:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I need to brainstorm a bit here regarding the Utf8CcsidManager class that I have. \\n\\n There\'s one thing that I didn\'t implement because of a detail regarding the following method: \\npublic String convertToUCS2(byte[] sourceBytes, int offset, int numToConvert) { } \\n\\n So far we had this method on the EbcdicCcsidManager and then it\'s fine because EBCDIC only uses one byte per character at all times. So the offset parameter always works in a consistent way, that is to say that if offset is 5, we are not only getting 5 sourceBytes but also getting exactly 5 characters. \\n\\n However, when we come to an Utf8CcsidManager, this offset might land straight in the middle of a character; then if we cut a character in half byte-wise, we will end with a totally different character. \\n\\n Is it acceptable to consider offset as a number of characters rather than a number of bytes? It works both ways in EBCDIC but for UTF8 it would mean converting the sourceBytes to a String, offsetting it character-wise, and then convert the \\u00ABoffsetted\\u00BB String to UCS2. \\n\\n Any other ideas anyone might have?              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv Espinha\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12878786_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Jun\\/10 22:51\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-06-14T22:51:54+0000\'\u003e14\\/Jun\\/10 22:51\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Here is the list of changes checked in by patch #2: \\n\\n \\n\\t Utf8CcsidManager.java is rolled in for the server - This CCSID manager is not yet really used in practice. Instances are created but no real live code refers to it yet. I\'m still unsure about this implementation and this code might change, but I needed to have a draft in place to proceed further. \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t Both DDMWriter and DDMReader now have three CCSID manager attributes. These two classes have one instance of each of the available managers (UTF-8 and EBCDIC) and a reference to the current enabled one (already part of the existing implementation). \\n \\n\\n\\n These two classes also no longer receive a CCSID manager in their constructor. Instead, they default to EBCDIC and whenever required we can setUtf8Ccsid() or revert to EBCDIC by doing setEbcdicCcsid(). \\n\\n \\n\\t The DRDAConnThread.java class has also lost its own ccsidManager and will be using the one from its instance of DDMWriter. This class now initializes its DRDAStrings within the initialize() method, as it is only then that we have a DDMWriter available. \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t Finally, the tests ProtocolTest and TestProto have also been changed to accommodate the constructor changes in DDMWriter and DDMReader. \\n \\n\\n\\n &#8211; \\n\\n I will be running regressions tonight. Provided that all goes well and there are no objections to this patch, it is ready for commit.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12878788\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-728?focusedCommentId=12878788&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12878788\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"espinha\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12878788_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=espinha\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"espinha\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Tiago R. Is it ok to muffle it and only deal with it on insane mode?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe second patch, DERBY_728_p3.diff, should in principle enable UTF-8 support in the server. I\'m not sure I\'ve missed something but I\'ll post a short explanation of what I\'ve done:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCodePoint.java\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nInserted the new code point for UNICODEMGR (0x1C08) as per the ACR and added it to the MGR_CODEPOINTS array.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&#8211;\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eNetworkServerControlImpl.java\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSet the minimum manager level for the UNICODEMGR in synch with the MGR_CODEPOINTS array.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&#8211;\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAppRequester.java\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSet the minimum manager level for the UNICODEMGR in synch with the MGR_CODEPOINTS array.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso added a convenience method that tells us whether the AppRequester depicted by this class supports or not UTF8. This relies on the manager level for UNICODEMGR being greater or equal to 1208. If the requester does not support UTF8, we won\'t get a UNICODEMGR manager level on the EXCSAT and as such UNICODEMGR will be set to 0 (which means this convenience method will return false).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&#8211;\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eDRDAConnThread.java\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nWhen dealing with the ACCSEC code point and after we send the ACCSECRD reply we check whether the appRequester supports UTF8 and if it does, we enable it through the switchToUtf8() method \u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;also part of the patch&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e. If it doesn\'t, make sure it goes back to EBCDIC, to make sure we aren\'t in UTF8 from the previous connection.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n&#8211;\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'m not sure how I\'d go about testing this as a client would have to support UTF-8 as well to be able to test it and this is still just the server side implementation. Espinha\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12883342_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'28\\/Jun\\/10 23:02\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-06-28T23:02:28+0000\'\u003e28\\/Jun\\/10 23:02\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I\'m attaching two patches to this issue. \\n\\n The first, DERBY_728_p2_sanity.diff aims at fixing an issue with sanity. I was making calls to the SanityManager without a check to verify that the DEBUG was enabled. A question that remains open is: what do we do with the exception on a sane build? Is it ok to muffle it and only deal with it on insane mode? \\n\\n\\n The second patch, DERBY_728_p3.diff, should in principle enable UTF-8 support in the server. I\'m not sure I\'ve missed something but I\'ll post a short explanation of what I\'ve done: \\n\\n \\n\\t CodePoint.java \\nInserted the new code point for UNICODEMGR (0x1C08) as per the ACR and added it to the MGR_CODEPOINTS array. \\n&#8211; \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t NetworkServerControlImpl.java \\nSet the minimum manager level for the UNICODEMGR in synch with the MGR_CODEPOINTS array. \\n&#8211; \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t AppRequester.java \\nSet the minimum manager level for the UNICODEMGR in synch with the MGR_CODEPOINTS array. \\n \\n\\n\\n Also added a convenience method that tells us whether the AppRequester depicted by this class supports or not UTF8. This relies on the manager level for UNICODEMGR being greater or equal to 1208. If the requester does not support UTF8, we won\'t get a UNICODEMGR manager level on the EXCSAT and as such UNICODEMGR will be set to 0 (which means this convenience method will return false). \\n&#8211; \\n\\n \\n\\t DRDAConnThread.java \\nWhen dealing with the ACCSEC code point and after we send the ACCSECRD reply we check whether the appRequester supports UTF8 and if it does, we enable it through the switchToUtf8() method  &#91;also part of the patch&#93; . If it doesn\'t, make sure it goes back to EBCDIC, to make sure we aren\'t in UTF8 from the previous connection. \\n&#8211; \\n \\n\\n\\n I\'m not sure how I\'d go about testing this as a client would have to support UTF-8 as well to be able to test it and this is still just the server side implementation. It will be a good test though to see if all regressions pass tonight; tomorrow, provided that this patch seems to be ok, I will do testing with older clients and see what the outcome is.
